  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c5e62c1f-fc1b-466e-9a95-c43176ea9d04'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

<span id="freeTextContainer7441270119042828513">It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn?   <span id="freeText7441270119042828513" style="display:none">It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn? In this anthology, edited by Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier (unicorn and zombie, respectively), strong arguments are made for both sides in the form of short stories. Half of the stories portray the strengths--for good and evil--of unicorns and half show the good (and really, really bad-ass) side of zombies. Contributors include many bestselling teen authors, including Cassandra Clare, Libba Bray, Maureen Johnson, Meg Cabot, Scott Westerfeld, and Margo Lanagan. This anthology will have everyone asking: Team Zombie or Team Unicorn?</span>

<div id="review_2313456354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2313456354" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2313456354?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2313456354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17825008176671883478">In a world dominated by <u>Sparkling Vampires</u> and <u>Hot Werewolves</u>, one dynamic duo dare to analyze the true question of our era - <b><u>Zombies VS Unicorns</u>.</b> <br/><br/><b>Twelve short stories</b> (each involving either Zombies or Unicorns) provide ample evidence for both sides, it is up to you to decide which one is truly better.<br/><br/><b><i>The highest justice </i>by Garth Nix</b> - Right off the bat we are toeing the line. An undead queen carried by a unicorn of death has one last wish - a kiss from her husband. Macabre and fun.<br/><br/><b><i>Love will tea</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText17825008176671883478" style="display:none">In a world dominated by <u>Sparkling Vampires</u> and <u>Hot Werewolves</u>, one dynamic duo dare to analyze the true question of our era - <b><u>Zombies VS Unicorns</u>.</b> <br /><br /><b>Twelve short stories</b> (each involving either Zombies or Unicorns) provide ample evidence for both sides, it is up to you to decide which one is truly better.<br /><br /><b><i>The highest justice </i>by Garth Nix</b> - Right off the bat we are toeing the line. An undead queen carried by a unicorn of death has one last wish - a kiss from her husband. Macabre and fun.<br /><br /><b><i>Love will tear us apart </i>by Alaya Dawn Johnson</b> - WOW. Just literally wow. This one is by far my fave of the set. Stay with me here - a gay zombie falls in love with the zombie hunter's son. I know. I know. I'm getting chills. It was so well written (and from second person to boot) and the characters are flawless. Alaya <b>
  <u>needs</u>
</b> to turn this one into a whole story<br /><br /><b><i>Purity test</i> by Naomi Novik</b> - Our homeless heroine is recruited by a unicorn for some very dastardly deeds. Very entertaining and for once, the virgin thing isn't so cut-and-dry.<br /><br /><b><i>Bougainvillea </i>by Carrie Ryan </b>- Iza and her family control one of last zombie free islands on earth. When a mysterious boy visits, Iza begins to wonder at what price her safety costs. <br /><br /><b><i>A thousand flowers</i> by Margo Lanagan</b> - We start with one very drink man looking for somewhere to pee. In his stupor, he managed to follow a unicorn and discover a passed out girl in a state of great distress. Nine months later something very peculiar happens. <br /><br /><b>The children of the revolution by Maureen Johnson </b>- whewww, a mother's love knows no bounds...but even so, you'd think she'd draw the line at zombifying children? Creepy and disturbing! <br /><br /><b><i>The care and feeding of your baby killer unicorn </i> by Diana Peterfreund </b>- Unicorns are back, they are hungry and meat is on the menu. Wen, a young girl, finds a baby killer unicorn and she doesn't have the heart to kill him. <br /><br /><b><i>Inoculata </i>by Scott Westerfeld </b>- One of the last human settlements is constantly surrounded by zombies. The teens in this one felt a little stereotypical-YA-winers but it wasn't too bad. The ending didn't make sense to me - too many plot holes. <br /><br /><b><i>Princess prettypants</i> by Meg Cabot</b> - What do you (a no-nonsense 17 yr old feminist) do when an aunt (rich, but distant) gives you a <i>unicorn</i> named Princess Prettypants? Obviously go on the most badass adventure possible! <br /><br /><b><i>Cold hands </i>by Cassandra Clare</b> - A town with a steady population of the undead. A murder covered up by a family. One, stunning conclusion. <br /><br /><b><i>The third virgin</i> by Kathleen Duey </b>- A unicorn with a death wish and serious substance abuse problems. Never thought I'd read about a junkie unicorn!<br /><br /><b><i>Prom night </i> by Libba Bray</b> - Hosting prom is stressful. Hosting prom using generators, scavenged decorations and stale snacks because the stupid zombie apocalypse happened is even worse. <br /><br /><b> Audiobook Comments </b><br />There were 3 readers for this one, which helped with high variety in tone / character in the short stories. The introductions to each story sounded wooden, but then again, they were a bit awkward to read too.<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17825008176671883478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_240589296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240589296" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240589296?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781441889256" href="/book/show/8754425-zombies-vs-unicorns">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Catie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240589296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2286578963791615741">Beatles vs. Rolling Stones. Cats vs. Dogs. Coke vs. Pepsi.<br/><br/>Zombies vs….<i>Unicorns?</i> Who knew? Apparently this is <i>the</i> divisive question of our time. And now, thanks to this anthology of stories, there’s a handy rubric for determining just how you should answer.<br/><br/>I listened to the audiobook, which was excellent. Phil Gigante, who some of you may be more familiar with as the voice of Jericho Z. Barrons, delivers many an eargasm as master of ceremonies. Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier provide their o</span>
  <span id="freeText2286578963791615741" style="display:none">Beatles vs. Rolling Stones. Cats vs. Dogs. Coke vs. Pepsi.<br /><br />Zombies vs….<i>Unicorns?</i> Who knew? Apparently this is <i>the</i> divisive question of our time. And now, thanks to this anthology of stories, there’s a handy rubric for determining just how you should answer.<br /><br />I listened to the audiobook, which was excellent. Phil Gigante, who some of you may be more familiar with as the voice of Jericho Z. Barrons, delivers many an eargasm as master of ceremonies. Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier provide their own rather nice voices for introductory/ back and forth banter at the beginning of each story, and the cast is pretty decent, with the major high point of Nick Podehl (aka, Todd Hewitt), and the major low point of Ellen Grafton (aka, Janie from Wake/Fade/Gone). <br /><br /><b>My Score Card:</b><br /><br /><u>The Mediocre</u><br /><br /><i>The Highest Justice</i> by Garth Nix<br />-Gruesome undead Queen with oozing pus and rotting limbs who just wants…a kiss: +2 stars<br />-Murderous Unicorns: +2 stars<br />-I forget if this is supposed to be a unicorn story or a zombie story: -1 star<br />-I think the author probably had his unpaid intern write this: -1 star<br /><br />A very boring, soporific start to the anthology. <b>2 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Purity Test</i> by Naomi Novik <br />-A nice play on the unicorn/virgin mythology: +2 stars<br />-A heroine who’s homeless, tough, and realistic: +2 stars<br />-Ellen Grafton makes her sound like she’s a scrappy twelve year old: -1 star<br />-Sounds like something I would write in a bout of silliness in one afternoon, and I’m a horrible writer: -1 star<br /><br />Forgettable and not very funny. <b>2 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Princess Prettypants</i> by Meg Cabot<br />-A unicorn who farts rainbows but can also turn into a fiery-eyed vengeance demon when necessary: +2 stars<br />-A cute, enjoyable story that is also about as deep as a mud puddle: +0.5 stars<br /><br />Sweet and funny, but barely scratches the surface of a premise that is actually pretty ripe with darker possibilities. <b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Cold Hands</i> by Cassandra Clare<br />-Even Justine Larbelestier (the head of team zombie) can’t keep herself from using the phrase “emo zombies” when referring to this story: -1 star<br />-A weird mish-mash of Victorian England and present day America that makes no sense: -1 star<br />-Zombies that actually aren’t all that different from regular ol’ people: -1 star<br /><br />A story about zombie civil rights…in the same way that Disney's The Little Mermaid is a movie about human civil rights. <b>-3 stars</b><br /><br /><u>The Middling</u><br /><br /><i>Bougainvillea</i> by Carrie Ryan <br />-Everything up to the ending: -1 star<br />-The ending: +4 stars<br /><br />Teen angst, over-descriptive prose, and lust/love in the midst of a zombie apocalypse…which is all mostly redeemed by that fantastic ending. <b>3 stars</b><br /><br /><i>The Children of the Revolution</i> by Maureen Johnson <br />-Angelina Jolie as a crunchy granola, immortality seeking weirdo +3 stars<br />-A narrator that’s likeable and amusingly clueless: +1 star<br />-Ellen Grafton makes her sound like she’s a scrappy twelve year old: -1 star<br /><br />A genuinely hilarious mockery of globe-trotting celebrities, their crazy religions, and their scores of adopted children. <b>3 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Prom Night</i> by Libba Bray <br />-Teenagers running society! +4 stars<br />-And they’re actually succeeding…there’s bartering, a police force, the prom…all the important things: -0.5 stars<br />-Boy serenades girl and it’s supposed to be sexy romantic: -0.5 stars<br /><br />This feels more like an introduction to a novel than a short story. It’s very classic Libba Bray, with a lot of sarcasm and bluster. I’m starting to realize that I’m not really a fan. <b>3 stars</b><br /><br /><i>Inoculata</i> by Scott Westerfeld<br />-Half zombie teenagers inherit the earth! +3 stars<br />-Lonely, snarky, independent main character who also happens to be a lesbian: +0.5 stars<br /><br />This one also feels more like an introduction to a series than a short story. AND, it’s very classic Westerfeld, with a foursome of teenagers set apart by paranormal abilities and born into a frightening world. My love for Scott Westerfeld is pretty much cemented by now so I would definitely read a full-length novel featuring these characters. <b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><u>The Masterful</u><br /><br /><i>Love Will Tear Us Apart</i> by Alaya Dawn Johnson<br />-2nd person perspective used well: +1 star<br />-m/m zombie “romance”: +1 star<br />-The fact that I needed to use quotes in the above tally (because this isn’t the gushy, I will love you forever type of romance): +1 star<br />-Nick Podehl has the most wonderful voice in the world: +1 star<br /><br />A gritty, emotional tale that breathes new life into the old “I want you but I also want to kill you” story. <b>4 stars</b><br /><br /><i>The Third Virgin</i> by Kathleen Duey<br />-A sort of Interview With the Unicorn: +1 star<br />-Creative twist on the unicorn healing mythology: +1.5 stars<br />-Nick Podehl puts on a very mediocre but adorable Welsh accent: +0.5 stars<br />-Use of the phrase “in a trice:” +0.5 stars<br /><br />A very unique idea that also manages to sound incredibly familiar. <b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn</i> by Diana Peterfreund <br />-Venomous, human-eating unicorns: +2 stars<br />-Thought-provoking religious and moral questioning: +1 star<br />-A boy named Eve: +0.5 stars<br />-Diana Peterfreund actually seems to know what a short story is: +1 star<br /><br />This is one of my favorites of the anthology. The main character’s incredible growth throughout the story is very moving. The ending is a nice punch in the gut; I wouldn’t be surprised if Diana Peterfreund is an experienced short story author. <b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br /><i>A Thousand Flowers</i> by Margo Lanagan<br />-Narration passed effortlessly between three points of view: +2 stars<br />-Nick Podehl puts on vaguely English accent: +0.5 star<br />-Beheadings, childbirth, suicide, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[bestiality. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>: +2 stars<br />-Why do unicorns like virgins so much? Oh. OOOOOOH. +1,000,000 stars<br /><br />The most genuinely creepy and haunting story of the bunch. Margo Lanagan somehow wrote a unicorn story that trumps every single zombie story in terms of genuine horror. Zombies seem downright cuddly now. <b>1,000,004.5 stars</b><br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />So let’s see. My final score is…*drumroll*<br /><br />Zombies: 13.5 stars<br />Unicorns: 1,000,014.5 stars<br /><br />So that means the winner is…ALL OF US, because we get to bask in the genius that is America.<br /><br />America – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=TdsmqwCRoM8" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Unicorn</a><br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/ya-review-zombies-vs-unicorns-edited-by-holly-black-and-justine-larbalestier.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2286578963791615741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3466311396" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3466311396" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3466311396?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=anthology">anthology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=unicorns">unicorns</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3466311396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7369121733843162799">Team Zombie started with one of the strongest stories in the book, but in the end it was Team Unicorn for the win. <br/><br/>The most dazzling contenders: <br/><br/>- "Love Will Tear Us Apart" by Alaya Dawn Johnson [Team Zombie]<br/>- "Purity Test" by Naomi Novik [Team Unicorn] <br/>- "A Thousand Flowers" by Margo Lanagan [Team Unicorn]</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_115920957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115920957" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115920957?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=nook-book">nook-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115920957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7576408718402527921"><i>Zombies Vs. Unicorns</i> and who is the winner?<br/><br/>Zombies! Thanks to Carrie Ryan's <i>Bougainvillea</i>. Undoubtedly the creepiest, most spine-tingly zombie story I have read since... well, since Ryan's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6468718.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>. Haters of that book shouldn't be dissuaded though. This story is lacking the angst and lurve triangles found in Forrest. Instead, we get complex, unique, sympathetic and believable characters in the midst of a zombie apocalypse. And of course a healthy dose of the zombie horror t</span>
  <span id="freeText7576408718402527921" style="display:none"><i>Zombies Vs. Unicorns</i> and who is the winner?<br /><br />Zombies! Thanks to Carrie Ryan's <i>Bougainvillea</i>. Undoubtedly the creepiest, most spine-tingly zombie story I have read since... well, since Ryan's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6468718.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>. Haters of that book shouldn't be dissuaded though. This story is lacking the angst and lurve triangles found in Forrest. Instead, we get complex, unique, sympathetic and believable characters in the midst of a zombie apocalypse. And of course a healthy dose of the zombie horror that Ryan does so very, very well. <br /><br />Notable zombie mentions include:<br /><br /> Maureen Johnson’s wonderfully bizarre <i>Children of the Revolution</i>, where we see something akin to a mix between old fashioned voodoo type zombies, new age religion and celebrity culture. Yeah, I know, it sounds like too much. But trust me, Johnson makes it work. <br /><br />Libba Bray’s <i>Prom Night</i> This is the woman who wrote<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3682.A_Great_and_Terrible_Beauty__Gemma_Doyle___1_" title="A Great and Terrible Beauty (Gemma Doyle, #1) by Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Great and Terrible Beauty</a>? It surprised me, because although I liked (<i>liked</i>, not loved) the first Gemma Doyle book, this dark, post-zombie apocalyptic story is not only better written, but so much more emotional and thought provoking. This one will stay with me for a long, long time. <br /><br />Not so awesome zombie entries include:<br /><br />Garth Nix’s <i>The Highest Justice</i> I’m not really sure whether this is Team Zombie or Team Unicorn, because it has a little of both. Either way, I didn’t care for it. <br /><br />Alaya Dawn Johnson’s <i>Love Will Tear Us Apart</i> I liked it but…. think Twillight: The Zombie Version. Granted, this is written so much better than Twillight. However, I can’t help thinking that the novel everyone loves to hate inspired this one. <br /><br />Scott Westenfeld’s <i>Inoculata</i> struck me as an introduction to a larger story, rather than a complete short. <br /><br />Cassandra Clare’s <i>Cold Hands</i> didn’t even belong here. Really. Zombie light. For kids. Kids who are not very discriminating readers. <br /><br />On the unicorn side, the case for their dominance and supreme scariness was very nearly won by Diana Peterfreund’s <i>The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn</i>. Silly title, no? Oh yeah, I agree. This is the first story I read from this collection. I know virtually nothing about Peterfreund’s writing (although I apparently know lots about her author-behaving-badly reputation) so I was more than a little curious to find out what kind of writer she is. This story blew me away. For a short story, there was an amazing amount of depth to it. Peterfreund created a complex and believable world in which unicorns ~ scary, evil <i>killer</i> unicorns exist. This was also a bit of a coming of age story, a romance story, and a little bit of religion thrown in as well. Yes, I know it seems like way too much. But it worked. I was hooked from the moment the young protagonist Wen sees a live unicorn at a circus side show… the unicorn growls… it’s handler grabs Wen’s arm and hisses to her, “You’re one of us” Oh gawd, I literally got chills at that moment and was reminded of the superbly creepy scene from <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0022913/" rel="nofollow noopener">Freaks</a> when everyone is chanting, “<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bBXyB7niEc0" rel="nofollow noopener">Gooble Gobble one of us, one of us</a>.” Long story short… I think I’m going to have to read some of Peterfreund’s work in the future. <br /><br />Notable unicorn mentions:<br /><br />Meg Cabot’s <i>Princess Prettypants</i> had the feel of a silly teen movie, but I loved it anyway. Just as light and fluffy as the title implies.<br /><br />Kathleen Duey’s <i>The Third Virgin</i> is dark, thought provoking and almost creepy enough to be a zombie story. Only there aren’t any zombies ;) <br /><br />Not so awesome unicorn stories are:<br /><br />Margo Lanagan’s <i>A Thousand Flowers</i> is very… typical of Lanagan. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What the fuck is it with this woman and bestiality??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was disappointed to find this story difficult to get into. She presented a vague world, and multiple points of view. I found the whole thing to be a bit messy and the story just never got a good flow.<br /><br />Naomi Novik’s <i>Purity Test</i> just didn’t do it for me. A little fantasy oriented a little snarky. Somehow this seemed to be lacking imagination. <br /><br />Like all anthologies, this was a mixed bag. But the great ones more than made up for the so-so stories. <i>Zombies Vs. Unicorns</i>, as so many people have said, is such a fantastic concept. I am kicking myself for not having read this collection sooner!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7576408718402527921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2030984377" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030984377" />
    <a title="Max Lau • Maxxesbooktopia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58160777-max-lau-maxxesbooktopia"><img alt="Max Lau • Maxxesbooktopia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606059190p2/58160777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030984377?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max Lau • Maxxesbooktopia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max Lau • Maxxesbooktopia" href="/user/show/58160777-max-lau-maxxesbooktopia">Max Lau • Maxxesbooktopia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/58160777-max-lau-maxxesbooktopia?shelf=4-stars-books">4-stars-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030984377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3246492416196302570"><b>
  <blockquote>“If you love someone, you’re not supposed to want them to come back. Better a peaceful sleep in the earth than the life of a zombie–not really dead but not really alive, either.”- Zombies Vs. Unicorns, Cassandra Clare.</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>My thoughts: Introduction</u>
</b><br/><br/>Let us start off with the introduction in each of the story that was presented in the book. Every introduction began with a heated conversation between Holly (Team Unicorn) and Justine (Team Zombie). Their conversations were mostly about how you sho</span>
  <span id="freeText3246492416196302570" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“If you love someone, you’re not supposed to want them to come back. Better a peaceful sleep in the earth than the life of a zombie–not really dead but not really alive, either.”- Zombies Vs. Unicorns, Cassandra Clare.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>My thoughts: Introduction</u>
</b><br /><br />Let us start off with the introduction in each of the story that was presented in the book. Every introduction began with a heated conversation between Holly (Team Unicorn) and Justine (Team Zombie). Their conversations were mostly about how you should switch your team to Team Zombie instead of Team Unicorn or how disgusting zombies really are. While I was reading the book, I looked forward on reading the introduction of each story because I enjoyed them and it made me laughed. I am sure you will laugh as well if you read the book!<br /><br />The plot of each story was unique and it proved how much time and effort the authors clicked the plot of their stories together! Some of the short stories in the book make me wish for a whole physical book dedicated to the stories I really want to read more about because some of them ended with a cliff-hanger and Oh my goodness, that’s not cool! I need more of them!<br /><br />The pacing for this book was not at all fast. It was slow in some stories and fast in the others. It took me 7 days to finish the book and this book was definitely worth the time! (Even though I kind of failed my June To-Be-Read Piles…)<br /><br />Some of the stories in the book dragged and let me tell you this: I did not enjoy the part where it dragged. We, as readers, tend to get bored when a story drags. So.. Yes, I did get bored and yawned a little at some point but I forced myself through those parts and the result is: I loved this book!<br /><br />But I did not enjoy all the stories in the book. Some stories that were written by Libba Bray, Garth Nix, Scott Westerfeld and Margo Lanagan felt flat to me. The characters did not really appeal to me in any way and there were quite a lot of unexplained things that bothered me throughout their stories. Bu-, but, I loved their writing style which I will talk more about later on, and I will, no doubt, be reading the work they published! <br /><br />Now, let us get on with the writing style!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Writing:</u>
</b><br /><br />For the writing style section, I will be doing it according to whose story was presented first, second, etc. For example, Garath Nix’s story was the first story that was presented in the book, so, I am going to talk about his writing style first.<br /><br />Team Unicorn: Garath Nix’s (Story Name: The Highest Justice) writing style for this book was great! It was simplistic, lyrical and articulate. Even though his story felt flat for me, I still want to read more from him and I can’t wait to read his other work beside Zombies Vs. Unicorns!<br /><br />Team Zombie: Alaya Dawn Johnson’s (Story Name: Love will tear us apart) writing style for this book was simply beautiful! I found her story to be intriguing because she writes like none other authors. She wrote ‘Love will tear us apart’ in second person point of view: you. It was weird and pretty uncomfortable in the beginning, but after a while, my love for the story and her writing style started growing and I ended up really enjoying the POV.<br /><br />Team Unicorn: Naomi Novik’s (Story name: Purity Test) writing style for this book was fabulous! I don’t think I can form a proper sentence… word, I mean, for her writing style.. So, I will just have to say that her writing style was fabulous.<br /><br />Team Zombie: Carrie Ryan’s (Story Name: Bougainvillea) writing style was awesome! I am going to read her other work soon. Her story and her writing style pulled me in until her story ended. (And I still cannot believe it ended that way.. [Spoiler])<br /><br />Team Unicorn: Margo Lanagan’s (Story Name: A Thousand Flowers) writing style was rare, I would say. Rare in saying how she changes point of views so quickly and professionally! Her story felt flat for me but her writing style totally did not!<br /><br />Team Zombie: Maureen Johnson’s (Story name: The Children Of Revolution) writing style and plot were oddly beautiful and touching. Firstly, Her writing style was as clear as the crystal… If you get what I am trying to say. Secondly, the plot of the story killed my heart and touched my heart with healing powers at the same time. I just can’t… That ending definitely destroyed me. (Sorry, I can’t tell you guys! I would be spoiling you if I have told you about the ending!)<br /><br />Team Unicorn: Diana Peterfreund’s (Story name: The care and feeding of your killer baby unicorn) writing style was very lyrical! Her writing style makes me want to read her other work, such as, ‘For Darkness Shows the Stars’ now! Her writing style was truly a work of art!<br /><br />Team Zombie: Scott Westerfeld’s (Story Name: Inoculata) writing style was not my favorite in this book. His writing style was a little inarticulate and a little too flowery but I am still looking forward on reading his other work even though I didn’t really like his writing style and the story!<br /><br />Team Unicorn: Meg Cabot’s (Story Name: Princess PrettyPants) writing style was fantastic! I did not really like her writing style in the beginning because I found it to be indirect, but I have grown to love her writing as the story progressed further. <br /><br />Team Zombie: Cassandra Clare’s (Story name: Cold Hands) writing style was great.. As always! Her story was bittersweet and I loved it! I will be reading ‘The Mortal Instrument’ Series soon! <br /><br />Team Unicorn: Kathleen Duey’s (Story name: The Third Virgin) writing style was clean and articulate. Basically, the plot of her story was about a unicorn becoming suicidal. Kind of weird because I have never thought of unicorns turning suicidal. Now, the story sticks in my head ever since I finished the book.<br /><br />Team Zombie: Libba Bray’s (Story name: Prom Night) writing style was consistence and fabulous! I loved her writing style, but unfortunately, the story she wrote felt flat for me.. But, I am still looking forward on reading ‘The Diviners’ book trilogy by her! <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Characters:</u>
</b><br /><br />For the characters section, I am just going to talk about a few characters in the book that I loved! So, let us get on with it!<br /><br /><b>Jess (From The Highest Justice):</b> She was a character that was brave, badass and kind. She is, no doubt, in my favorite characters list and I wish we can have a physical book fully dedicated to her and her trials in the throne. <br /><br /><b>Grayson (From Love will tear us apart):</b> She is definitely the best character in the book! She had a great character growth in a short story. She was not kind and not a good person. That’s all I am going to talk about her because I do not want to spoil the surprise for you guys!<br /><br /><b>Iza (From Bougainvillea):</b> She had… a great character growth but the character growth came crashing down at the end of the story. To be honest, I kind of died off a little because she had potential but she turned into what her [Spoiler] was. But, all in all, I still loved her.<br /><br /><b>Wen (From The Care and Feeding of your Baby Killer Unicorn):</b> She was pretty weak in the beginning, but her character growth increased as the story proceeded. Wen was kind, a little annoying, brave and adventurous! I loved her character in this book!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall:</u>
</b><br /><br />I am giving this book an 80% rating. I loved it and I recommend you all to check this book out! <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>“She feels like someone has planted a tree in her chest and then pressed fast foward on the world, branches growing and twisting and pushing her apart from the inside.”- Zombies Vs. Unicorns, Carrie Ryan.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />This review is also posted at <a href="https://maxxesbooktopia.wordpress.com/2017/07/01/zombies-vs-unicorns-by-holly-black-and-other-collective-authors/" rel="nofollow noopener">Maxxesbooktopia: Zombies Vs. Unicorns by Holly Black and other collective authors</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3246492416196302570" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_192069035" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192069035" />
    <a title="Meggy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5918544-meggy"><img alt="Meggy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1313193997p2/5918544.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192069035?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meggy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meggy" href="/user/show/5918544-meggy">Meggy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192069035" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18404232923859596512">Probably the worst anthology I've ever read. The stories themselves weren't that bad, although some of them were pretty... out there. Not many of them made sense or kept to the overall theme of the actual collection. And I don't mean that I expected the stories to be about zombies and unicorns having it out, but I expected the stories to at least center around zombies and/or unicorns. But the majority of the stories only mentioned unicorns or zombies briefly. The zombie stories were the worst of</span>
  <span id="freeText18404232923859596512" style="display:none">Probably the worst anthology I've ever read. The stories themselves weren't that bad, although some of them were pretty... out there. Not many of them made sense or kept to the overall theme of the actual collection. And I don't mean that I expected the stories to be about zombies and unicorns having it out, but I expected the stories to at least center around zombies and/or unicorns. But the majority of the stories only mentioned unicorns or zombies briefly. The zombie stories were the worst offenders, as many of them were just about people living in camps or compounds and the undead were only mentioned at the beginning or end of the stories. The editors' remarks were really what made the collection horrible, though. Holly Black manages to write paragraphs while managing to say nothing at all, and Justine Larbalestier was an absolute harpy. Just insult after insult (all in "good fun", I'm sure) to "Team Unicorn" and being an outright brat made me put down the book and shake my head numerous times. Overall, the stories are lackluster, the editors incompetent, and the appeal severely lacking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18404232923859596512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer10392003468918965018">Zombies... <br/><br/>Unicorns...<br/><br/>How could this possibly go wrong?<br/><br/>I mean, they're just so awesome!<br/><br/>I'll review what I've read so far and update as I go.<br/><br/>The Highest Justice by Garth Nix.<br/><br/>Nix! You're one of my favourite authors! This story was kind of awesome in that I felt like this should have been the beginning to one of your amazing big adventure series. Instead, just as it got started and became exciting, it ended! It was too big an idea squeezed into too small a story that you just couldn't do it the jus</span>
  <span id="freeText10392003468918965018" style="display:none">Zombies... <br /><br />Unicorns...<br /><br />How could this possibly go wrong?<br /><br />I mean, they're just so awesome!<br /><br />I'll review what I've read so far and update as I go.<br /><br />The Highest Justice by Garth Nix.<br /><br />Nix! You're one of my favourite authors! This story was kind of awesome in that I felt like this should have been the beginning to one of your amazing big adventure series. Instead, just as it got started and became exciting, it ended! It was too big an idea squeezed into too small a story that you just couldn't do it the justice it deserved. Also the unicorn was a Dues Ex Machina. <br /><br />Inoculata by Scott Westerfeld<br /><br />*Blinks* What the...<br /><br />The chic/chic love was awesome and the CONCEPT of the innoculation was awesome... but that was the beginning to an amazing story. Not a short story. I mean... what was with that ending? It wasn't even an ending!<br /><br />The Purity Test by Naomi Novik<br /><br />*Laughs and falls over*<br /><br />Okay, chica, I'm going to go find what you've written and read it. That's just win!<br /><br />Bougainvillea by Carrie Ryan<br /><br />Nice. Very nice. Good and emotive writing too! You're another one I might have to go check out. <br /><br />Okay - will update when I've read more.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_134520356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134520356" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134520356?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      YA book club
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=book-club">book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=short-stories-poetry-collections">short-stories-poetry-collections</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134520356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer316779294756827848">I'm a sucker for amusing zombie stories. No really, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/245891-zombie-wedding' rel='nofollow noopener'>I am</a>. And I grew up on <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0084237/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Last Unicorn</a>, bad singing and all. So when I heard of the concept of this book, what makes better fiction, zombies or unicorns? I had to smile. What a fun idea for a short story anthology.<br/><br/>I cracked the cover thinking "zombies for the win, all the way." I <i>never</i> laugh when I read, crack a smile at most, but not laugh. The introduction alone, a debate between editors <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30033.Justine_Larbalestier' title='Justine Larbalestier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Justine Larbalestier</a> about the benefit</span>
  <span id="freeText316779294756827848" style="display:none">I'm a sucker for amusing zombie stories. No really, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/story/show/245891-zombie-wedding" rel="nofollow noopener">I am</a>. And I grew up on <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0084237/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Unicorn</a>, bad singing and all. So when I heard of the concept of this book, what makes better fiction, zombies or unicorns? I had to smile. What a fun idea for a short story anthology.<br /><br />I cracked the cover thinking "zombies for the win, all the way." I <i>never</i> laugh when I read, crack a smile at most, but not laugh. The introduction alone, a debate between editors <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30033.Justine_Larbalestier" title="Justine Larbalestier" rel="nofollow noopener">Justine Larbalestier</a> about the benefits of zombies and unicorns, had me laughing out loud. Oh the stories that could fill this anthology. So who won my heart? Team zombies or team unicorns? Here's the fickle trail of my loyalty:<br /><br />1. The Highest Justice by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix" title="Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Garth Nix</a>. The most interesting thing about this story was the titillation of a zombie appearance. It was okay, had the flair of a medieval unicorn story but without any of the mystique of the medieval creatures. I think Nix should have stuck to team zombie and left the description of unicorns to someone who wanted to write about them.<br /><br />2. Love Will Tear Us Apart by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/546427.Alaya_Dawn_Johnson" title="Alaya Dawn Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">Alaya Dawn Johnson</a>. The story started out crass with way too many f words. I'm not a fan of crass humor (or the f word), not even a little. The zombie POV with descriptions of his virus as a psychopathic disorder were awesome and the battle of love vs zombie feeding was good too (Twilight-esque without the cheese), but all that crassness made me feel dirty and I never recovered from it. Plus, I'm not a fan of same-sex romances. I know zombies are gross, but they can be funny or scary without the crass factor, right? Maybe I don't want to be on team zombie.<br /><br />3. Purity Test by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8730.Naomi_Novik" title="Naomi Novik" rel="nofollow noopener">Naomi Novik</a>. Score one for humor. Jokes about finding a virgin in NYC, Harry Potter, and how dragons are so much cooler than unicorns, which begs the question: dragons or vampires? Sequel, anyone? Midway through it fizzled and got old, but a team unicorner who has a sense of humor about unicorns, maybe I'm switching teams.<br /><br />4. Bougainvillea by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1443712.Carrie_Ryan" title="Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">Carrie Ryan</a>. We already know Ryan can write a best seller about the zombie apocalypse. Couldn't she surprise us with a good unicorn story? Or even a different zombie story? Okay the story was interesting and memorable (beside the tense shifts that drove me crazy), but zombie apocalypse, dictatorship keeping the last remaining humans intact, rebellious teenager, haven't we read this before, from her?<br /><br />5. A Thousand Flowers by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/277536.Margo_Lanagan" title="Margo Lanagan" rel="nofollow noopener">Margo Lanagan</a>. The POV shifted in the middle of the story, dropping the only character I connected with. Several vague explanations and descriptions later (not a fan of the writing), we learn that the point of unicorns is not to save the wrongly accused, to heal the princess child, to avenge the robbery of her purity, but beastiality, and a romance that leaves a lot of victims in its wake (including its readers with those graphic images in our head, not only beastiality, but with a child, nice). What ever happened to the magical creatures that were supposed to be the point of this anthology? Are they ever going to make an appearance? Definitely team zombie at this point.<br /><br />6. The Children of the Revolution by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10317.Maureen_Johnson" title="Maureen Johnson" rel="nofollow noopener">Maureen Johnson</a>. A satire about celebrity-adopted children "cured" from death by a zombie virus. Tom Cruise on his no medication media rant, Angelina Jolie adopting yet another child, celebrities who don't actually raise their children, I'll let you decide what Johnson is mocking. Either way, the satire made me smile. I knew there was a reason I was team zombie.<br /><br />7. The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119848.Diana_Peterfreund" title="Diana Peterfreund" rel="nofollow noopener">Diana Peterfreund</a>. If I can't get a magical unicorn the way they are depicted in medieval fiction, I'll take a killer, wild-animal version with the <s>vampire</s> unicorn slayer who just can't kill them. Another story that tied into the mythology and storyline of her novel, even more so, but since I haven't read it, I didn't have the same expectation for new creativity I did with Ryan. A strong story and protagonist. I'm not discounting team unicorn just yet.<br /><br />8. Inoculata by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13957.Scott_Westerfeld" title="Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Scott Westerfeld</a>. I was into this story until it just ended, a flat, empty, quitting of words because it'd already gone on too long. Westerfeld tried to make a quick, enlightening statement, or maybe just make me think about zombies a different way, but it didn't work for me. (There's some girl-on-girl action, same girl later going for some girl-on-boy action. It is in vogue these days.) The story was just developing when it ended, leaving me to wonder if maybe there just weren't any more good zombie stories out there. My loyalty is in limbo.<br /><br />9. Princess Prettypants by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot" title="Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Meg Cabot</a>. Again with the sense of humor about unicorns. None of team zombie have touched humor (except Johnson with her satire that's not nearly as strong as this story). Cabot says, yeah okay, so unicorns are the obnoxious fairytales of little girls, but if one showed up on your doorstep, would you actually turn it away (or sell it on ebay) or would use that fierce, magical power to intimidate your ex-boyfriend? Oh yeah, and happy endings aren't so bad either. Mock all you want, you know deep down, you'd love a unicorn. Score one for team unicorn.<br /><br />10. Cold Hands by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/150038.Cassandra_Clare" title="Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Cassandra Clare</a>. Not having read the Mortal Instruments series myself, I had heard that Clare's writing was atrocious, but I found her writing in this quite beautiful. Her zombies aren't the brain-sucking types, just undead cursed to return from the grave seeking out the company of their loved ones, making the love story not quite the moral dilemma of Johnson's story, but I still liked it. It's a sweet zombie love story. I'm still open to either team.<br /><br />11. The Third Virgin by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/179733.Kathleen_Duey" title="Kathleen Duey" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen Duey</a>. I liked the idea of this psychopathic <s>zombie</s> unicorn story more than I liked the all-tell, no-show delivery of it. I find myself wondering if any of the team unicorn writers actually like unicorns.<br /><br />12. Prom Night by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2526.Libba_Bray" title="Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">Libba Bray</a>. A story about zombies on prom night? I am so there. Only, that's not what this story was about. Another zombie apocalypse, this one where the adults got infected and only children survived, and as their food and hope runs out, they hold prom. Not a bad story (although Bray once again pushes the "I know what teens are like" display too far), but it wasn't quite the story I'd wanted to read when I know Bray is capable of humor and zombies on prom night lend themselves to it.<br /><br />There was no zombie/unicorn showdown. None of the unicorns I'd expected showed up and there wasn't enough humor in the zombie stories. Each team had a story that left a bad taste in my mouth, but there were plenty that shined, which is rather difficult with a short-story anthology. So who won? Team zombie or team unicorn. I'd have to say the editors. Their commentary was hands down the best part of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="316779294756827848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_95059888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95059888" />
    <a title="Ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/726203-ellen"><img alt="Ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226546692p2/726203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95059888?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen" href="/user/show/726203-ellen">Ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/726203-ellen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/726203-ellen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/726203-ellen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/726203-ellen?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/726203-ellen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95059888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13489935536936672249">I'm not a big anthology reader, because there are usually as many stories I don't like as ones I do, and it's easy to put them down between stories. As far as I can recall, I liked every single story in <i>Zombies vs. Unicorns</i>, and I couldn't put it down even between stories. Chances are, if you're a YA SFF reader, there are at least a few authors in here you love; there was only one name I didn't recognize.<br/><br/>Special mentions to Naomi Novik's awesome New York-set unicorn story; Diana Peterfreund's co</span>
  <span id="freeText13489935536936672249" style="display:none">I'm not a big anthology reader, because there are usually as many stories I don't like as ones I do, and it's easy to put them down between stories. As far as I can recall, I liked every single story in <i>Zombies vs. Unicorns</i>, and I couldn't put it down even between stories. Chances are, if you're a YA SFF reader, there are at least a few authors in here you love; there was only one name I didn't recognize.<br /><br />Special mentions to Naomi Novik's awesome New York-set unicorn story; Diana Peterfreund's contribution set in the <i>Rampant</i> universe; and Maureen Johnson's creepy zombie baby-sitting story, which I was reading on the subway when someone sat down next to me and I jumped about two feet in the air. Oh, and Garth Nix's, which is the only one that <i>actually</i> pits a zombie against a unicorn. (The unicorn wins.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="13489935536936672249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129007874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129007874" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/520753-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402541317p2/520753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129007874?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/520753-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=the-kids-are-all-right">the-kids-are-all-right</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=it-was-density">it-was-density</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=and-i-feel-fine">and-i-feel-fine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/520753-kim?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129007874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11111055386622951260">There are so many great rivalries in history. Ahab vs. the Whale, Edison vs. Tesla, Hamilton vs. Burr, Coke vs. Pepsi, boxers vs. briefs... Wolfe vs. Mailer... Goodreads vs. Everyone <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Hey, look what I found about author put downs! <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.examiner.com/article/the-50-best-author-vs-author-put-downs-of-all-time'>http://www.examiner.com/article/the-5...</a> Just a thing, no heated debate needed, thought it was neat is all)  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br/><br/>Of course, there would be <a href='http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gv7V1u0FBXo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Zombies vs. Unicorns</a>.<br/><br/>Rightfully so. Back in my pre pubescent(and I will say it, 'chaste') days, unicor</span>
  <span id="freeText11111055386622951260" style="display:none">There are so many great rivalries in history. Ahab vs. the Whale, Edison vs. Tesla, Hamilton vs. Burr, Coke vs. Pepsi, boxers vs. briefs... Wolfe vs. Mailer... Goodreads vs. Everyone <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Hey, look what I found about author put downs! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.examiner.com/article/the-50-best-author-vs-author-put-downs-of-all-time">http://www.examiner.com/article/the-5...</a> Just a thing, no heated debate needed, thought it was neat is all)  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />Of course, there would be <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gv7V1u0FBXo" rel="nofollow noopener">Zombies vs. Unicorns</a>.<br /><br />Rightfully so. Back in my pre pubescent(and I will say it, 'chaste') days, unicorns rocked. My little pony, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29127.The_Last_Unicorn__The_Last_Unicorn___1_" title="The Last Unicorn (The Last Unicorn, #1) by Peter S. Beagle" rel="nofollow noopener">The Last Unicorn</a>, those velvet paintings at the flea markets with sparkly depictions (this was pre-Lisa Frank). It was a special time. I won't wince when I use the word 'pure'. I would later call it 'guilded-cage' syndrome, but what have you.<br /><br />My Johnnie Rotten/Charles Bukowski/Joy Division days didn't give much thought to either Unicorns or Zombies. Wasn't my thing... Zombies ate brains, they weren't depressed little beings..... and I haven't really considered the rivalry so pressing in my little bubble. <br /><br />Then you bring in the YA authors. The newer crop who give us these buffet king like offerings (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5530930.Geektastic_Stories_from_the_Nerd_Herd" title="Geektastic Stories from the Nerd Herd by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Geektastic: Stories from the Nerd Herd</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/493569.21_Proms" title="21 Proms by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">21 Proms</a>) --ooh, look, they have some Scott Westerfield... should I mix that with some Barry Lyga or will that give me an upset stomach? John Green? No way! Double that! and I will definitely be having some Libba Bray for dessert!---<br /><br />And now I have to choose between zombies and unicorns. Sigh.<br /><br />Zombies won. Out of the 12 stories, I liked more of the zombie ones than the unicorns... but this isn't saying that the unicorns didn't make me laugh or cry or anything... I guess that as I've aged, I've discovered I have more in common with zombies.<br /><br />Which presents a whole bunch more of discussion at therapy next week.<br /><br />My favorites: <b>'Love will tear us apart' by Alaya Dawn </b> -you had me at Joy Division, but kept me at Squeeze. <br /><br /><b>'Children of the Revolution' by Maureen Johnson</b> because the idea of Brangelina have zombie children just fucking rocked.<br /><br /><b>'Cold Hands' by Cassandra Clare</b> because I love a good doomed but not love story. And the prince sounded really hot.<br /><br /><b>'Inocula' by Scott Westerfield</b> because aren't we all zombies inside, just a little?<br /><br /><b>'Prom Night' by Libba Bray </b> because I love Libba Bray and I love hope when there isn't a future for it. <br /><br />I will gives props to <b>'Princess PrettyPants' and 'The Third Virgin'</b> for not making me hate unicorns and bringing back just a little bit of that worship.<br /><br />In all, please keep these anthologies a-coming. I love you guys. Don't quit me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11111055386622951260" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122669442" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122669442" />
    <a title="stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86145-stephanie"><img alt="stephanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1181278917p2/86145.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/122669442?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="stephanie" href="/user/show/86145-stephanie">stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=would-rec">would-rec</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/86145-stephanie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122669442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14646893990207956185">so, i'm not really a huge fan of short story collections, as i'm not really a fan of short stories. however, a lot of my favorite YA authors have chosen this year to be part of anthologies (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119848.Diana_Peterfreund' title='Diana Peterfreund' rel='nofollow noopener'>Diana Peterfreund</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1192311.Claudia_Gray' title='Claudia Gray' rel='nofollow noopener'>Claudia Gray</a>, i'm looking at you!), i have found myself reading more of them. <br/><br/>which makes them a little hard to review - having so many different stories and authors. <br/><br/>however, i think this is the best collection i've read in a long time. first of all, you have zombies, which usually means t</span>
  <span id="freeText14646893990207956185" style="display:none">so, i'm not really a huge fan of short story collections, as i'm not really a fan of short stories. however, a lot of my favorite YA authors have chosen this year to be part of anthologies (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/119848.Diana_Peterfreund" title="Diana Peterfreund" rel="nofollow noopener">Diana Peterfreund</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1192311.Claudia_Gray" title="Claudia Gray" rel="nofollow noopener">Claudia Gray</a>, i'm looking at you!), i have found myself reading more of them. <br /><br />which makes them a little hard to review - having so many different stories and authors. <br /><br />however, i think this is the best collection i've read in a long time. first of all, you have zombies, which usually means the end of the world, which of course i love. and then you have killer unicorns, which thanks to ms. peterfreud, are the coolest things ever. <br /><br />i remain fully on team unicorn, though <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13957.Scott_Westerfeld" title="Scott Westerfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Scott Westerfeld</a>'s zombie story, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1443712.Carrie_Ryan" title="Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">Carrie Ryan</a> (come on, she like invented zombies) as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8347.Garth_Nix" title="Garth Nix" rel="nofollow noopener">Garth Nix</a>'s (truly creepy - wait, that might have been a unicorn story too) were stand-outs on the zombie side. <br /><br />but when you have a baby unicorn in a cardboard box in a garage who you know is a man-eating monster, another unicorn named (i kid you not) <em>PRINCESS PRETTYPANTS</em> who actually FARTS RAINBOWS, is there really a chance? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11654.Meg_Cabot" title="Meg Cabot" rel="nofollow noopener">Meg Cabot</a>, i love you too. <br /><br />plus it was edited well, though i think justine did a much better job defending zombies than holly did with unicorns. but that's probably just because unicorns haven't always been scary, while zombie have. going against the grain! <br /><br />conclusion: enough stories that i don't think you should miss to read it. (winners: diana peterfreund, meg cabot, garth nix, scott westerfeld, carrie ryan. major winners.)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14646893990207956185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99437881" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8480115989109360830">Anthologies are so difficult to review because they're a mixed bag, ya know? So even though this anthology had a handful of brilliant stories I'd have to say it was all sullied by a short story that contained bestiality. Oh, yeah, and all the zombie romances--between zombies and humans (What the what?!). Ew. And so, so wrong. So wrong. <br/><br/>If I have time I'll review each short story separately. <br/>***<br/>Why it has taken <i>this long</i> for such a book to be conceived and written is beyond me. I know I've spent </span>
  <span id="freeText8480115989109360830" style="display:none">Anthologies are so difficult to review because they're a mixed bag, ya know? So even though this anthology had a handful of brilliant stories I'd have to say it was all sullied by a short story that contained bestiality. Oh, yeah, and all the zombie romances--between zombies and humans (What the what?!). Ew. And so, so wrong. So wrong. <br /><br />If I have time I'll review each short story separately. <br />***<br />Why it has taken <i>this long</i> for such a book to be conceived and written is beyond me. I know I've spent many a night contemplating which would win in a battle to the death (or, in the case of Zombies, second death), Zombies or Unicorns. <br /><br />Seriously though, I really am excited to read this anthology. Call me a dork--I don't care. The book description is incredibly amusing and a lot of my favorite authors have contributed, so I'm willing to bet this book is nothing but <b>FULL OF WIN</b>. </span>
