    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_325670260" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325670260" />
    <a title="Aubrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey"><img alt="Aubrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472535045p2/4119460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/325670260?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aubrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aubrey" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey">Aubrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=antidote-think-twice-all">antidote-think-twice-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=person-of-everything">person-of-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=antidote-think-twice-read">antidote-think-twice-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=1-read-on-hand">1-read-on-hand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=r-goodreads">r-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reality-check">reality-check</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=person-of-reality">person-of-reality</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer325670260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1173986298228651689">It's a sad fact that the transformation from child to adult is commonly defined as the growth in both ability and instinct to put books such as this down not for reasons of the work inciting genocidal hatred or solidifying the accompanying trigger-happy fragility complexes of the all too able, but for being rather silly, or limited, or kitsch in scope. Therefore, I don't take especial pride in noting that the majority of these do not appeal, but only take comfort in the fact that I did my best t</span>
  <span id="freeText1173986298228651689" style="display:none">It's a sad fact that the transformation from child to adult is commonly defined as the growth in both ability and instinct to put books such as this down not for reasons of the work inciting genocidal hatred or solidifying the accompanying trigger-happy fragility complexes of the all too able, but for being rather silly, or limited, or kitsch in scope. Therefore, I don't take especial pride in noting that the majority of these do not appeal, but only take comfort in the fact that I did my best to give each story its due, critiquing on the basis not of fanciful topic, but level of writing, however demographically-teen. The hilarious thing is, Holly Black, the author who haunted my teen/young adult/not so young adult years, doesn't even feature in this other than as an editor and erstwhile prefacer, and I refuse to count her over the top bantering as a quality reread of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__Modern_Faerie_Tales__2_" title="Valiant (Modern Faerie Tales #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a>. Slightly frustrating, but she isn't the only name I recognized out of past familiarity or glancing always-passed-the-books-on-the-shelves-by reference, so it was a nostalgic, if varied in reward, sojourn through the fantasy of my youth.<br /><br />Despite the fact that the subject material is such a hit or miss (although I wonder what the authors would make of the zombie resurgence still swamping entertainment in various cinematic forms), there is a surprising amount of middle ground. No 5's, but this has as much to do with my inherent dislike of the short story format and its tendency to tie together loose ends too neatly as it does to evaluation of various technical flaws. The 4's go to 'Bougainvillea' by Carrie Ryan, wonderfully written as well as skillfully balancing the fine line between novel world building and the short and sweet of a short story, and 'A Thousand Flowers' by Margo Langan, so well crafted and tantalizing in its diving deep into the land of sexual taboo (and I'm not talking any variation of the same-species canoodling here) that I have to wonder how anyone who's read this passes this off as entirely for teenagers. The same holds for 3 star 'Love Will Tear Us Apart' by Alaya Dohn Johnson (also an example of the appreciably substantial amount of queerness) and 2.5 star 'Cold Hands' by Cassandra Clare, both of which touch upon, you guessed it: necrophilia. One could technically make a similar argument for 2 star 'The Children of the Revolution' by Maureen Johnson, but does it count if they're both dead? Anyway, to return to the threes, Garth Nix is one of my absolute favorites (I think only a story by Philip Pullman, or Holly Black herself of course, would have appealed more), but his 'The Highest Justice' was too straightforward to merit anything higher than a 3. 'Purity Test' by Naomi Novik, 'Inoculata' by Scott Westerfield (bonus star for the queerness), and 'Prom Night' by Libba Bray (bonus star for Zoroastrianism and actual Iranian people participating in it) all garnered 2s for not doing anything out of the ordinary while reasonably entertaining, while 'The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn' by Diana Peterfreund, 'Princess Prettypants' by Meg Cabot, and 'The Third Virgin' by Kathleen Duey got 1 stars for including such things as Christocentricity, normalization of rape culture, and ableism without even providing a decent story to make up for it. I suppose 'The Third Virgin' can get a half a star more, but the whole wander-thousands-of-years-in-a-supposed-frontier-aka-US-till-only-succeed-when-white-people-get-there is a bit much.<br /><br />I wish I had read this back in 2010, or at least whenever I first acquired it, as I've grown too used to the calcification of "proper" literature to push for as much queerness as I encountered amongst these supposed immaturities. It would've probably done me some good, and I would've gotten more out of watching the rise of 'The Walking Dead' and the White Walkers and 'The Last of Us' and 'World War Z' and every other zombie iteration of a possibly leveling off yet still innovatively engaging fad. As it stands, I'm hellbent on getting a proper Holly Black at my next sale, as that is one I experienced at the right time that I'm highly curious about reexperiencing and reevaluating. Other than that, it's time to move on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1173986298228651689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_123201743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123201743" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1347278-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371914212p2/1347278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123201743?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/1347278-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123201743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14540007979624740553">I resisted reading this one for awhile, because 1) I'm not a big fan of short story collections in general and 2) while I love zombies, I couldn't understand the appeal of dedicating half the collection to unicorns.<br/><br/>Seeing the epic debate over the merits of zombies vs. unicorns in NYC, however, changed my mind, and I am SO GLAD I picked up this collection. Most of the unicorn stories are somewhat tongue in cheek, and with a collection of authors like these, I really never should have doubted the </span>
  <span id="freeText14540007979624740553" style="display:none">I resisted reading this one for awhile, because 1) I'm not a big fan of short story collections in general and 2) while I love zombies, I couldn't understand the appeal of dedicating half the collection to unicorns.<br /><br />Seeing the epic debate over the merits of zombies vs. unicorns in NYC, however, changed my mind, and I am SO GLAD I picked up this collection. Most of the unicorn stories are somewhat tongue in cheek, and with a collection of authors like these, I really never should have doubted the quality of stories for either team.<br /><br />On Team Zombie, my favorite stories were Scott Westerfeld's, set in an abandoned pot farm where the adults are losing it while the kids think the zombies are essentially no big deal, and Maureen Johnson's, where a celebrity adherent to a weird religion has turned her adopted kids into zombies as part of a religious rite. Carrie Ryan's story, set in the same world as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead Tossed Waves</a> was a great addition to that world, too. For Team Unicorn, I really liked Naomi Novik's unicorn who isn't too careful about finding virgins in Central Park, and Meg Cabot's avenging unicorn. Diana Peterfreund's story is set in her already existing killer unicorns universe, and has almost convinced me that I need to hunt down those other books. The story works well on its own, but I was constantly wondering if these characters had a bigger life in the other novels or if, like in Carrie Ryan's story, these were all-new characters set in a familiar world.<br /><br />Justine Larbalestier and Holly Black introduce each story with a good deal of bickering. Justine is much more hostile towards unicorns than Holly is towards zombies. Holly is just creeped out by zombies, while Justine sees unicorns as offensive. It's great.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14540007979624740553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1237217303" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1237217303?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1237217303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2204007430971500530">I honestly didn't get this book. Was it even really necessary? <br/><br/>Plain and simple, it's a collection of stories for geeks, nerds and comic book salesmen alike. I honestly think it was trying to rake it in off the recent zombie apocalypse subgenre popularity and the whole "brony" fad from that god-awful <i>My Little Pony</i> show. Before zombies and unicorns, it was vampire romances. In about five years something else will be the new trend, probably elves, faeries or talking donkeys. I'd rather not think </span>
  <span id="freeText2204007430971500530" style="display:none">I honestly didn't get this book. Was it even really necessary? <br /><br />Plain and simple, it's a collection of stories for geeks, nerds and comic book salesmen alike. I honestly think it was trying to rake it in off the recent zombie apocalypse subgenre popularity and the whole "brony" fad from that god-awful <i>My Little Pony</i> show. Before zombies and unicorns, it was vampire romances. In about five years something else will be the new trend, probably elves, faeries or talking donkeys. I'd rather not think about it.<br /><br />I think this book was supposed to be funny, but I read all the stories and honestly didn't see the humor in it, just a lot of off-topic nerd trivia and choppy writing. </span>

<div id="review_114777777" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114777777" />
    <a title="Kai Charles(Fiction State Of Mind)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1583976-kai-charles-fiction-state-of-mind"><img alt="Kai Charles(Fiction State Of Mind)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582570844p2/1583976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/114777777?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai Charles(Fiction State Of Mind)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai Charles(Fiction State Of Mind)" href="/user/show/1583976-kai-charles-fiction-state-of-mind">Kai Charles(Fiction State Of Mind)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer114777777" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer627902280798501265">It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn? In this anthology, edited by Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier (...more It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn? In this anthology, edited by Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier (unicorn and zombie, respectively), strong arguments are made for both sides in the form of short stories. Half of the stories portray the strengths--for good and evil--of unicorns and half sho</span>
  <span id="freeText627902280798501265" style="display:none">It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn? In this anthology, edited by Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier (...more It's a question as old as time itself: which is better, the zombie or the unicorn? In this anthology, edited by Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier (unicorn and zombie, respectively), strong arguments are made for both sides in the form of short stories. Half of the stories portray the strengths--for good and evil--of unicorns and half show the good (and really, really bad-ass) side of zombies. Contributors include many bestselling teen authors, including Cassandra Clare, Libba Bray, Maureen Johnson, Meg Cabot, Scott Westerfeld, and Margo Lanagan. This anthology will have everyone asking: Team Zombie or Team Unicorn? Cover Blurb<br /><br /><br />I Loved this Anthology! First, lets get this out of the way, I'm 100% TEAM ZOMBIE! Since there are twelve stories in this anthology:<br />six zombie/six unicorn, I've decided to review them in a head to head smackdown! Let's see who is triumphant!<br /><br /> ROUND ONE<br /> The Highest Justice vs Love Will Tear Us Apart<br /><br />Garth Nix's story: The Highest Justice: interesting tale.<br />It also has a necromanced zombie! Princess Jess is bringing her recently reanimated mother to confront her father the King. She has invoked the help of the Unicorn Elibet, a silent tool of vengeance that has been attached to her family for generations.<br /><br />The purpose of their journey is to confront the King and his sorcerous mistress who Jess suspects is responsible for her mother's death. <br /><br />The story is well written and dispels the gentle unicorn myth.<br /><br /><br />Alaya Dawn Johnson gives us : Love Will Tear Us Apart. A very sweet and funny tale of Phillip Grayson a teen zombie. Phillip begins to hang out with the uber popular jock,Jack. Phillip's feelings for Jack straddle the line between intense hunger and an even intenser physical attraction. Jack seems to reciprocate these feelings but both of them are hiding deep secrets that threaten their slowly growing love.<br /><br />I loved the dark humor and teen angst in Alaya's story. It was also unique to see a Gay protagonist. I really felt attached to the characters and was rooting for them to get together.<br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM ZOMBIE !!<br /> <br /> <br /> ROUND TWO!<br /><br /> Purity Test vs Bougainvillea<br /><br />I'm a huge fan of Naomi Novik's Temeraire books so I was excited to see her take on Unicorns. Young Allison has been rudely awakened from her nap on a Central Park bench, by a Unicorn horn poke! She is confused and hungover as she takes in the irritable talking Unicorn Belcazar. Belcazar is on a mission to rescue some baby unicorns and has demanded Allison be his companion, despite her lack of virginity :) I loved this story! so much fun. Allison and Belecazar have great chemistry between them, even though it's sarcastic and argumentative.<br /><br />Carrie Ryan's Bougainvillea is a story set in the same world as the book The Forest Of Hands And Teeth. Iza is the daughter of a powerful Govenor on the island of Curacao. She feels trapped in her life despite its many comforts. One rash decision up ends her life and forces her to make decisions about her future. I enjoyed learning a little bit more about the world after the Return. Iza is an interesting character and i'd like to see more of her in a future story. The zombie action is a little brief but intense!<br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM UNICORN !!<br /> <br /> ROUND THREE<br /> A Thousand Flowers vs The Children of the Revolution<br /><br />I struggled with Margo Lanagan's story : A Thousand Flowers. Set in ancient times, it starts out interesting enough. A young man comes across a unicorn. Entranced he follows the Unicorn and comes across a beautuful young princess lyng on the ground. She has obviously attacked. Trying to help her the young man, Manny is captured by the King's guard. When the Princess declares him innocent he is released, until several month later when he is hunted down. It has become discovered the Princess is pregneant.At this point the story fell apart for me. It becomes obvious who the source of the child is . The narrative also shifts abruptly and the ending is anti clamatic.<br /><br /><br />Children of the Revolution: Maureen Johnson. What was supposed to be a romantic farm vacation in England turns into a nightmare for college student Sofie. Abandoned by her boyfriend Franklin, Sofie takes a Babysitting job with a reclusive celebrity that will fund her way home. These aren't ordinary children though, and one simple act of compassion changes Sofie's life. This was an enjoyable story, not action packed but a definite twist ending.<br /><br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM ZOMBIE!!<br /> <br /> ROUND FOUR<br />The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn vs Inoulata<br /><br />Dina Peterfreund's story is set in the same universe of her Novel Rampant. Unicorns have returned to the world,and they aren't happy! They are vicious man eaters.The main character Wen has experience with them. In fact she is irrestible to them, she witnessed them attack and kill her cousins . Now barely a year later she is at a carnival freak show with some friends. The carnival advertises a live unicorn called Venom. Wen's friends think it's fake but once Wen is in the tent she instantly knows it isn't. <br /><br />Wen can feel the unicorns emotions, read it's thoughts and has fantastic powers when she is in a unicorn's presence.This link draws her back to the circus where she witnesses Venom give birth and plead with Wen to rescue her baby. <br /><br />This is a marvelous story! My heart raced when I read it! Wen experiences a deep struggle with her choice to save little "Flower". She struggles with what her faith and her parents would expect her to do vs what her heart is asking of her. Beautifully written. It has made me RUSH to read Diana's book Rampant.<br /><br />In Scott Westerfeld's story Inoculata a small group of teens and adults are living on a secure farm. The watch the evergrowing numbers of undead who surround their fences day and night. Young Allison also watches Kayln, a beautiful young girl who she is in love with. One night while talking to Kayln she discovers a shocking secret that changes the lives of everyone in the camp. Nicely told and an interesting take on infection and survival in an undead world.<br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM UNICORN!!<br /> <br /> ROUND FIVE<br /> <br /> Princess Prettypants vs Cold Hands<br />Meg Cabot's Princess Prettypants is about Liz Freelander's seveenth birthday. In a day that steadily is going from bad to worse she is shocked to find her big gift of the night is a Unicorn shipped to her by her eccentric Aunt. This was a fun story. Meg deftly chronicles the High School terrain and sets up a series of events that lead to a fun climactic ending and a little romance :)<br /><br />Cold Hands is the love story of James and Annie. the have been childhood pals and are expected to be engaged until an accident tears them apart. Loved ones rarely stay gone in the English town of Lychgate, and a courageous act by Annie may be the key to their reunion.<br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM ZOMBIE!!<br /> <br /> ROUND SIX<br /> <br /> The Third Virgin vs Prom Night<br /><br />The Third Virgin by Kathleen Duey examines the healing powers of Unicorns. It narrates the 500 year journey of a Unicorn that cannot die or be killed. It's healing prowess is immense, but he also has the power to withdraw the life force of those he touches. The spark he feels with this act is the only true joy he gets in his existence. His desire becomes an addiction ,coupled with a cruel streak of deception and manipulation of his virgin companions.His "third virgin" Ree bears internal and external scars due to a family tragedy. As the unicorn heals her he also lays a emotional trap for her that may lead to pain and death. This was a wonderful and disturbing story. Kathleen explores how time, isolation and addiction might shape the perspective of an already alien creature. <br /><br />Prom Night by Libba Bray has the feel ofLord Of The Flies with braiiins. There is little zombie action but ,the threat is immenient. Instead the story focuses on Jeff and Tahmina, the "police" in a small fenced in town abscent of adults. The teens move thru their year with as much normalcy as possible, including hosting a Prom. A very interesting tale examining teen relationships and the abscence of adults in their world.<br /><br /> WINNER? TEAM UNICORN!!<br /><br />A Tie!!! I have to create a bonus category for the wonderful introductions/debates/rivalry's by the wonderful Holly Black and Justine Larbalestier before each chapters. Based on that the over all winner in this Battle Royale is :<br /> TEAM ZOMBIE!!!!<br /> As if there was any doubt :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="627902280798501265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1281696290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281696290" />
    <a title="Maya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20362530-maya"><img alt="Maya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491403295p2/20362530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1281696290?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maya" href="/user/show/20362530-maya">Maya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20362530-maya?shelf=rant-review">rant-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20362530-maya?shelf=summer-reading">summer-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20362530-maya?shelf=good-but-bad">good-but-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20362530-maya?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20362530-maya?shelf=what-is-going-on">what-is-going-on</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1281696290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10588060170582760030">So I'll do that thing I do when I review anthologies: review them by short stories. I mean, what other way is there? You may have absolutely hated one (NEGATIVE ONE STAR!) But loved another (1000 STARS!!:D) So I give each story the right to be represented. YEAH! So let's get on with it!!<br/><br/>The Introduction: Yeah, I know it wasn't a short story, but I really enjoyed it anyway. I like those authors. So it was fun to read! Read funny introduction! Yes! I don't know why I'm talking like that...<br/><br/>The High</span>
  <span id="freeText10588060170582760030" style="display:none">So I'll do that thing I do when I review anthologies: review them by short stories. I mean, what other way is there? You may have absolutely hated one (NEGATIVE ONE STAR!) But loved another (1000 STARS!!:D) So I give each story the right to be represented. YEAH! So let's get on with it!!<br /><br />The Introduction: Yeah, I know it wasn't a short story, but I really enjoyed it anyway. I like those authors. So it was fun to read! Read funny introduction! Yes! I don't know why I'm talking like that...<br /><br />The Highest Justice: 3 stars<br />Umm, it was pretty good. It was short, that's for sure. It didn't seem to have that much of a story arc to me. It felt like a snippet from a longer book. That's the thing with short stories (and it's hard): you have to make sure you don't unknowingly make it a snippet from a novel. <br /><br />Love Will Tear Us Apart: 3.5 stars <br />That was good too, though not mind blowing. It was slightly confusing. Did Grayson die at the end? How did he not eat? He's gonna turn into a raging maniac! The concept was pretty interesting, though. <br /><br />Purity Test: 5 stars<br />That's what I'm talking about!!! This was hilarious, had a proper story arc, was awesome, had unicorns, and did I mention that it was hilarious? Or that it had unicorns? Yeah. The best one so far!! I want more of these! <br /><br />Bougainvillea: Four stars (because of the writing.)<br />It made me slightly sick, which I think was the aim. <br />This reminded me heavily of The Walking Dead. Guy walks in, takes over, calls himself the Governor, becomes a ruthless psycho. Area becomes overrun, mass murder commences. It was depressing and creepy and it didn't have Chandler Riggs in it. No me gusta. <br /><br />The creepy thing I didn't see coming was her becoming the psycho dictator. It was sad and creepy but unfortunately not unrealistic. <br /><br />Team Unicorn 4 Life! <br /><br />A Thousand Flowers: -1 stars<br />Ew. EW! EWEWEWEWEW! EWWWWWWWW!!!! <br />I can't unread that. I am scarred for life. Future readers, I would highly suggest you skip this story. It is confusing and nasty. <br /><br />The Children of the Revolution: 5 stars<br />Oh my goodness oh my goodness! That was really creepy and scary. That would make a really good horror movie. It's 2:16 in the afternoon and I'm still freaked out. Super scary, just like a zombie story should be. Also disturbing. Did I mention disturbing? It was disturbing. <br /><br />The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn: 4 stars<br />That was interesting, entertaining, and I told myself that when it was over I had to do my math homework. Which I really don't want to do but I've been procrastinating all weekend...<br /><br />Inoculata: 4.5 stars<br />Nice job as usual, Scott Westerfeld. Gripping, melancholy, all that a zombie story should be. I enjoyed that very much, as much as you can enjoy a bittersweet tale of the undead. I suppose it's a different kind of enjoyment.<br /><br />Princess Prettypants: 4.5 stars<br />Oh how I love Meg Cabot. She is just so fun and sparkly and awesome- Just like this story! It was super satisfying and that unicorn totally kicked ass, almost literally. And that High School Musical party...I lol'd. <br /><br />Cold Hands: 5 stars<br />THAT'S WHAT I'M TALKING ABOUT. Yes. This is a fantastic zombie story. Fantastic. I loved it. The romance, the mystery, the action, the narration, the fact that Cassandra Clare wrote it...all awesome. This is definitely one of the best stories in the book. <br /><br />The Third Virgin: 3.5 stars<br />Well, that was interesting and all, but it was hella depressing. It was beautiful and all, but it was hella depressing. It was a unique take on the unicorn story, which I appreciated, but it was hella depressing. <br /><br />Prom Night: 4 stars <br />Another very interesting take on the apocalypse. I enjoyed it. It sort of reminded me of a zombie version of Under the Dome. I tried to read that last summer, and wish it was a short story like this was. Or even a shorter story. I mean, it had over a thousand pages. This didn't, though, and it was a good story!<br /><br />So, who is the winner of this battle? I was Team Unicorn at the beginning, but am I still? Time for some averaging! <br /><br />On average, I rated unicorn stories 3.16 stars. It think it was my rating for A Thousand Flowers that brought it down so much. <br /><br />On average, I rated zombie stories 4.33 stars. <br /><br />Does this mean zombies win? It depends on how how you think about it. If I decide the winner based on which of the two I think is better, then I'd obviously choose unicorns. I mean, zombies are awful (except for the ones in Cold Hands). They kill people and change people in more ways than one. They do carry diseases! They're ugly and insanity and murderous. Unicorns are beautiful but powerful healers and fighters for justice. They are awesome. I had unicorn wallpaper in my room when I was a little kid. I was a unicorn for Halloween. I had a stuffed unicorn named Daisy. Unicorns rock. <br /><br />If I decide the winner based on which would win in a fight, unicorns would also win. That horn. Plus they can heal from injuries. So pretty much undefeatable. Don't even try to argue with me here. <br /><br />People who know me would say, "But Maya, you love The Walking Dead. How are you on Team Unicorn?" It's true. The Walking Dead is one of the best shows ever. I love it. But the zombies aren't the reason I love it. I don't love the zombies. I love Carl, Daryl, Glenn, Beth, Maggie, Rick...the people. <br /><br />But despite all I just said, math states that I liked the zombie stories more on average. This is true, because of the disturbing quality of some of the unicorn stories. You'd have thought that the zombie stories would be the disturbing ones, but no. Unicorns aren't just rainbow sparkles. <br /><br />I come to the conclusion that, even though unicorns are better than zombies, this book didn't make me think that, nor that zombies are worse. Just like the Walking Dead isn't good because of the zombies, these stories aren't good or bad because they have unicorns or zombies in them. They don't really show if one is better, just which stories are good or bad or all right. Does that make sense? Probably not. <br /><br />I liked this book. The authors are cool. You should read it if you want to looks at unicorns and/or zombies in a different way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10588060170582760030" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68425982-sydney-s?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer12739909636192182680">I don't think I was the right audience for this. The book itself is a beautiful hardback with a gorgeous cover (not with the black on it like in the thumbnail) but that's about the only thing I liked about this collection of short stories. I read this one so fast only because I was basically skimming the stories after the first 3 stories I read at random were just so damn boring. I'm disappointed in the authors, who are known for writing some pretty popular fantasy or horror books. I was really </span>
  <span id="freeText12739909636192182680" style="display:none">I don't think I was the right audience for this. The book itself is a beautiful hardback with a gorgeous cover (not with the black on it like in the thumbnail) but that's about the only thing I liked about this collection of short stories. I read this one so fast only because I was basically skimming the stories after the first 3 stories I read at random were just so damn boring. I'm disappointed in the authors, who are known for writing some pretty popular fantasy or horror books. I was really hoping to love this because I've been wanting to read more short stories after loving <i>The Language of Thorns,</i> but this book almost put me in a reading slump. I wouldn't say I'm a big unicorn fan, and I really have never found zombies to be interesting, so maybe it's my own fault for buying this book in the first place. <br /><br />The concept was cool, and I like that there's commentary from the editors in between each story, but as a whole this collection feels so lazy and thrown together. Like the writers just did not care at all. If you love unicorns and zombies, maybe you'll like this collection. I just honestly think the stories were pointless and boring on their own. </span>

<div id="review_2778558312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2778558312" />
    <a title="Amanda Kratz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65751558-amanda-kratz"><img alt="Amanda Kratz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492453986p2/65751558.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2778558312?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda Kratz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda Kratz" href="/user/show/65751558-amanda-kratz">Amanda Kratz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2778558312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6643999505769440214">So this is actually an interesting premise. A few authors got into an argument on one of their online message boards about which creatures were better Zombies or Unicorns. They then decided to write stories about them and compile them into a book. There is #TeamZombie & #TeamUnicorn. Several very silly tales with many popular authors you may recognize like Holly Black, Cassandra Clare, Scott Westerfeld, Naomi Noviak, Meg Cabot & many others.<br/><br/>Here are brief thoughts about the short stories contain</span>
  <span id="freeText6643999505769440214" style="display:none">So this is actually an interesting premise. A few authors got into an argument on one of their online message boards about which creatures were better Zombies or Unicorns. They then decided to write stories about them and compile them into a book. There is #TeamZombie &amp; #TeamUnicorn. Several very silly tales with many popular authors you may recognize like Holly Black, Cassandra Clare, Scott Westerfeld, Naomi Noviak, Meg Cabot &amp; many others.<br /><br />Here are brief thoughts about the short stories contained within. I will give each story a score of 1-5 stars to see which wins #TeamUnicorn or #TeamZombie (Because why not?)<br /><br />Team Unicorn:<br /><br />The Highest Justice by Garth Nix: - I always find Garth Mix’s writing just a bit young for my tastes. This is a quick story about a young princess who’s mother is a zombie being brought before the king for justice. It’s just too short and too random really to judge it harshly. I always expect these stories to have a funny ending or a surprise twist and this was straight forward. ⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Purity Test by Naomi Novik - so the premise of this one is imagine you got so sloppy drunk and passed out in Central Park only to be awoken by a unicorn who needs you help. Quick and cute. I’d like to see where else it went. ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />A Thousand Flowers by Margo Lanagan - There are somethings you just can’t unread this is one of them. It warns you before but yes there is beastiality in this story we don’t really see it but at the same time you know - full on Catherine the great. Yeah not for me. ⭐️<br /><br />The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn by Diana Peterfreund - Who doesn’t want a pet unicorn? Only instead of a cute fluffy ball of joy they were a man eating pile of rage? Would you still want one? This is cute kinda leaves on a cliff hanger. I’d like the next chapter please. ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Princess Prettypants by Meg Cabot - Ah finally a cute sweet story! Yay unicorns and rainbows and non zombie romances! And who wouldn’t want a unicorn for a birthday present? ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />The Third Virgin by Kathleen Duey - In my opinion the most disturbing story of the book. That’s right the unicorn story is more bothersome than all the zombies. We all know unicorns are magical, but what if that magic had a dark cost(whether real or assumed is the question). I really liked this one. It has some interesting viewpoints at the end despite its twisted Ness. ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Team Zombie:<br /><br />Love Will Tear Us Apart by Alaya Dawn Johnson - Hilarious!!! It’s kind of what I’d imagine Edward Cullen was thinking as he kissed Bella Swan. This is a quick, dark, humorous, tale of a zombie boy in love with a zombie hunter boy. The ending felt a bit rushed but I would love to see more works by this author! ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Bougainvillea by Carrie Ryan - This short story is a bit of a jumbled mess but I like the dark twisted ending. The story keeps hopping back and forth between the past and present and really seems kinda all over the place but the ending is spot on! ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />The Children of the Revolution by Maureen Johnson - so imagine if Angelina Jolie went around adopting zombies children and then hired a nanny to care for them. That is the premise of this short story. A lot of weird drowning on about the nanny’s boyfriend, but not bad. ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Inoculata by Scott Westerfeld - so there is a zombie infection and you’ve managed to survive for years. Your crush says hey I got bitten but I’m not a zombie I’m going to infect you and maybe you’ll be immune too. - A recipe for disaster if you ask me ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Cold Hands by Cassandra Clare Well we had beastiality on team unicorn, why not necrophilia on team zombie. A story of murder and betrayal, but in a town where the dead can rise can you get away with your crimes? ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />Prom Night by Libba Bray - Prom &amp; Zombies. Although to be fair other than the events occurring on prom night there wasn’t much prom in the story. I expected more of a Carrie vibe but still one of the darker stories in the collection⭐️⭐️⭐️<br /><br />So in the end we have #Team Unicorn at 19 ⭐️s and #TeamZombie at 20⭐️s. (Wow I didn’t realize it would be that close I thought Team Zombie was dominating) while I do prefer unicorns over zombies The proof is in the stars Zombies are just more fun to write about.<br /><br />Who do you think should win #TeamZombies or #TeamUnicorn?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6643999505769440214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_79687296" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/79687296" />
    <a title="Crowinator" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator"><img alt="Crowinator" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604950964p2/283407.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/79687296?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crowinator" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crowinator" href="/user/show/283407-crowinator">Crowinator</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=magical-creature-menagerie">magical-creature-menagerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=genre-horror">genre-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/283407-crowinator?shelf=zombieland">zombieland</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer79687296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7482309327305587978">I guess Black and Larbalestier have been debating the merits of zombies vs. unicorns on the Internet for a while now, but I missed the hoopla until it finally spilled over into this anthology of twelve stories. At first, I thought that each story would be a death match between a zombie and a unicorn, but that would have gotten old fast, so I’m glad instead that each author represents a side: on Team Zombie, it’s Alaya Dawn Johnson, Carrie Ryan, Maureen Johnson, Scott Westerfeld, Cassandra Clare,</span>
  <span id="freeText7482309327305587978" style="display:none">I guess Black and Larbalestier have been debating the merits of zombies vs. unicorns on the Internet for a while now, but I missed the hoopla until it finally spilled over into this anthology of twelve stories. At first, I thought that each story would be a death match between a zombie and a unicorn, but that would have gotten old fast, so I’m glad instead that each author represents a side: on Team Zombie, it’s Alaya Dawn Johnson, Carrie Ryan, Maureen Johnson, Scott Westerfeld, Cassandra Clare, and Libba Bray; on Team Unicorn, it’s Garth Nix, Naomi Novik, Margo Lanagan, Diana Peterfreund, Meg Cabot, and Kathleen Duey. <br /><br />The two editors, Holly Black pulling for unicorns and Justine Larbalestier for zombies, duke it out in the introductions to each story. These “arguments” lose their charm and get repetitive quickly, because when it comes right down to it, there isn’t much to say about zombies vs. unicorns that isn’t handled better just by reading the stories. I’m not saying that some of these intro pieces are not funny, because they are, but as a cumulative effect they grow boring. Still, it doesn’t cost much to read them, and they do introduce points of contention in the zombies vs. unicorn debate (for example, is it more interesting that zombies represent society’s political or social illnesses, or that unicorns paradoxically symbolize both virginity and raw sexuality?). <br /><br />I’ve read a lot of zombie stories (and seen a lot of movies), but my experience with unicorns is more limited: Peter S. Beagle’s <i>The Last Unicorn</i>, which I don’t remember well as a novel or a cartoon from my childhood; Holly Black’s short story “Virgin”, and . . . that’s about all I can remember. So, I was actually looking forward to reading the unicorn stories, just to see what’s out there in the modern day, but I ended up on Team Zombie anyway. I don’t know if I find zombies more interesting because I enjoyed the stories more, or if I enjoyed the stories more because I find zombies more interesting, but it’s still the case: overall, the zombies won out. <br /><br />I liked all of the zombie stories in this collection, but my top ones were: “The Children of the Revolution”, by Maureen Johnson, the zombie babysitting story which was funny and creepy and had a killer ending; “Bougainvillea”, by Carrie Ryan, which is set in the same universe (after the Return) as her two novels and continues her excellent storytelling; and “Prom Night”, by Libba Bray, which had a subtle, disquieting ending as doomed teenagers, after all of the adults in town have been quarantined or killed, attempt to soldier on with the high school tradition of prom. <br /><br />For the unicorn stories, the only one I really cared for was “The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn”, by Diana Peterfreund, which is set in her <i>Rampant</i> universe and definitely made me want to read the novel. Several of the stories explored the dangerous side of unicorns, but this was the one I felt did it best. I also enjoyed Meg Cabot’s “Princess Prettypants” as a kind of as tongue-in-cheek, light-hearted revenge fantasy, and I thought two of the others – Margo Lanagan’s and Kathleen Duey’s – were both disturbing in a good way. (I’ve come to expect that from both of them, though I’ll admit that as someone who admires Lanagan’s short stories, I was kind of disappointed in her entry.)<br /><br />Both sides of the debate concerned themselves with issues of power, violence, and sexual desire (or should I say, sexual hunger?), but I thought it was curious that a lot of the zombie stories I liked had a strong romance element, involving zombies of various sentience levels, while several of the unicorn stories focused more on their dangerous side, often as a vengeful judge/punisher of wrongdoing.<br /><br />Cover comments: Honestly, this book should sell based on the cover design alone. The cut-out of the zombie fighting a unicorn, and the cartoonish but graphically violent scenes of their death match ranging over hill and dale, is some of the best I’ve seen. Not only does it effectively present the focus of the book, it’s hilarious and eye-catching. It's like looking at an <i>I-Spy</i> or <i>Where's Waldo</i> book, but with a sick twist.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7482309327305587978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_151005343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151005343" />
    <a title="Brittany" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92397-brittany"><img alt="Brittany" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191511794p2/92397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151005343?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/92397-brittany">Brittany</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/92397-brittany?shelf=yafantasy">yafantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151005343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14432640569240473379">This was a book with a very important premise: Which is cooler, zombies or unicorns? The whole debate, and the deeply entrenched opinions on each side, are wonderfully reminiscent of the great astronauts vs. cavemen debate (on this, as in almost everything else, I'm Team Angel. Er, I mean Team Astronaut). Two authors, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30033.Justine_Larbalestier' title='Justine Larbalestier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Justine Larbalestier</a> lead two teams of authors, Team Unicorn and Team Zombie respectively, in writing stories. The stated purpose was to determine which were cooler</span>
  <span id="freeText14432640569240473379" style="display:none">This was a book with a very important premise: Which is cooler, zombies or unicorns? The whole debate, and the deeply entrenched opinions on each side, are wonderfully reminiscent of the great astronauts vs. cavemen debate (on this, as in almost everything else, I'm Team Angel. Er, I mean Team Astronaut). Two authors, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/30033.Justine_Larbalestier" title="Justine Larbalestier" rel="nofollow noopener">Justine Larbalestier</a> lead two teams of authors, Team Unicorn and Team Zombie respectively, in writing stories. The stated purpose was to determine which were cooler. The real purpose, of course, was to create a fun romp of an anthology. They succeeded.<br /><br />Each story was introduced by both Holly and Justine discussing how this story tips the balance toward or away from their chosen team. The banter was extremely amusing, and reminded me of many similar debates I've had with my friends over the years.<br /><br />To no one's surprise whatsoever, I came down firmly on the side of Team Unicorn. Holly's opinions pretty much echo my own: I don't care for shambling, disease, or the walking dead. I liked best the zombie stories where I could pretend they were "some other kind of undead thing I like." (Holly rocks, by the way. I must find more books by her. Or invite her to my next party.) <br /><br />I had to grit my teeth to get through the creepy zombie stories. Eugh. But I loved the unicorn stories (even the upsetting ones). <br /><br />The thing is, I understand Team Zombie's point of view. Zombies are a great metaphor for human society. They are entropy made animate and a perfect cipher for commercialism, materialism, and soullessness. But I <i>just don't like them</i>. I like unicorns. Even the ones whose farts smell like rainbows, and who live in Fairyland, and prefer virgins as company. It's the same as the way that I can recognize that lots of music is much more sophisticated and deep and worthy than my happy country music; I just like country music and unicorns better. (I feel like I ought to burst into a rendition of "Fireflies" by Patty Griffin. Or, even better, Faith Hill.) <br /><br />I want all my friends to read this book, so I can see if my guess of who would be which team is correct.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14432640569240473379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The fact that while I love unicorns I am not a fan did not help my ratings when it comes to the Team Zom</span>
  <span id="freeText10073545697751775672" style="display:none">Overall, this was a weird anthology. The commentary before each short story was cringey at best and awful at worst, I think it was supposed to be funny? While I like the idea of that I found the execution to be terribly lacking.<br />As for my general enjoyment... there were only two stories that really stood out to me ( Love Will Tear Us Apart and The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn). The fact that while I love unicorns I am not a fan did not help my ratings when it comes to the Team Zombie stories.<br /><br /><u>The Highest Justice - Garth Nix</u><br />★★✩✩✩<br />I was not a fan, the combination of unicorns and zombies felt weird to me and I don't think it's something to mix together. Fucking hilarious apparently. A bit chopped up since the story had so many interlides but it was quite worth my while.<br /><br /><u>Purity Test - Naomi Novik</u><br />★★✩✩✩<br />Love the name Belcazar. The story? Not so much.<br /><br /><u>Bougainvillea - Carry Ryan</u><br />★★★✩✩<br />Interesting and unusual. I did not care at all.<br /><br /><u>The Children of the revolution</u><br />★★★✩✩<br />Cults are always creepy and it doesn't get any better if you add zombie children to it.<br /><br /><u>The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn - Diana Peterfreund</u><br />★★★★✩<br />Hilarious. Uniquely twisted and funny. (Also I enjoyed the fact that this was not a love story.)<br /><br /><u>Inoculata - Scott Westerfeld </u>- 2 stars<br />★★✩✩✩<br />Weird?!<br /><br /><u>Princess Prettypants by Meg Cabot</u><br />★✩✩✩✩<br />I hate the lore of these unicorns, not my fan.<br /><br /><u>Cold hands by Cassandra Clare </u><br />★★★✩✩✩<br />Mafia in Zombietown. Enjoyable.<br /><br /><u>The third virgin by Kathleen Duey</u><br />★★★✩✩<br />I wasn't a fan exactly of the beginning but I quite liked the turn it took and the exploration of eternal life.<br /><br /><u>Prom night by Libba Bray</u><br />✩✩✩✩✩<br />dnf. Again, I didn't care.</span>

<div id="review_273903820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/273903820" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/273903820?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer273903820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13020253622334166601"><b>Note:</b> As part of Zombies vs Unicorns month, I will be updating this with the new stories that I review. They will be reviewed in "bunches" (2+ reviewed together). The rating will be from what I have read so far (so it may change)<br/><br/><b>Review of Inoculata by Scott Westerfeld & Cold Hands by Cassandra Clare</b><br/>From Uglies and Mortal Instruments... to zombies! Seems like everyone is converting to zombies! I don't blame them, team zombie really is where it's at! <br/><br/>Scott Westerfeld and Cassandra Clare's stories </span>
  <span id="freeText13020253622334166601" style="display:none"><b>Note:</b> As part of Zombies vs Unicorns month, I will be updating this with the new stories that I review. They will be reviewed in "bunches" (2+ reviewed together). The rating will be from what I have read so far (so it may change)<br /><br /><b>Review of Inoculata by Scott Westerfeld &amp; Cold Hands by Cassandra Clare</b><br />From Uglies and Mortal Instruments... to zombies! Seems like everyone is converting to zombies! I don't blame them, team zombie really is where it's at! <br /><br />Scott Westerfeld and Cassandra Clare's stories have something in common, and that something is also what was discussed in Lia Habel's guest post last week - they both make it clear that zombies are not dumb! From George Romero's slow, sluggish, mindless flesh-eaters, to the 28 Days Later or Zombieland zombies who are capable of intelligent thoughts, are fast and self-aware. Yep, zombies have evolved. They can even become boyfriend material - although that still raises eyebrows if you really think about it. The point is : zombies are underestimated. Scott and Cassandra have both brought up this evolution in their stories. One considers that zombies are simply bored, while the other has them living amongst humans like old friends who smell. <br /><br />As my first venture into this book of zombies and unicorns anthologies, I was satisfied and amused. I picked both of these first because I have a fondness of their previous work and found myself super curious how they would write zombies. I found the Scott story pretty entertaining - I even wished it was novel-length. It definitely has a really intriguing concept. As for the Cassandra story, it was passable. It felt very weak as far as the zombie "world-building". I could think of quite a few plot holes behind the zombie existence. Regardless, it was still light and fun.<br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127878685" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17084221251724743582">When I began, I thought for sure that I would be Team Zombie! Well, I think that I am still Team Zombie, but I must admit that I have more respect for unicorns now. As shown in some of the stories, they would be useful pets. <br/><br/>My favorite story was "Children of the Revolution", a zombie story. The best unicorn stories were "Princess Prettypants" and "The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn". <br/><br/>The worst stories were "Thousand Flowers" and "Highest Justice". They were 1. really stupid, and 2</span>
  <span id="freeText17084221251724743582" style="display:none">When I began, I thought for sure that I would be Team Zombie! Well, I think that I am still Team Zombie, but I must admit that I have more respect for unicorns now. As shown in some of the stories, they would be useful pets. <br /><br />My favorite story was "Children of the Revolution", a zombie story. The best unicorn stories were "Princess Prettypants" and "The Care and Feeding of Your Baby Killer Unicorn". <br /><br />The worst stories were "Thousand Flowers" and "Highest Justice". They were 1. really stupid, and 2. boring. "Thousand Flowers" really was kind of disturbing and gross in a way, too... In "The Third Virgin", it kind of gave an anti-unicorn feel, although it was supposedly was Team Unicorn. That was one mean and messed up unicorn.<br /><br />It was also funny to see Justine and Holly's commentary before every story. It really gave more life to the book. I wish that they had more of a conclusion to the book after the final story, however.<br /><br />Overall, this book was very entertaining, humourous, and unique! Read it and decide for yourself: which is better- the zombie(dramatic pause)or the unicorn!</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/201024929?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer201024929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8512002848587783375">This book was one of the best fantasy books I've ever read. It has all the perfect stories compiled all in one book. The things I like best about reading books with lots of short stories is that if you don't like one or is getting tired of it, its over withen the chapter. Also it has just great sarcastic/humerous writing throughout it and I feel that keeps it fresh. This book goes through all the stereotypical thoughts about Unicorns and Zombies. Then it steps out into a complete different zone,</span>
  <span id="freeText8512002848587783375" style="display:none">This book was one of the best fantasy books I've ever read. It has all the perfect stories compiled all in one book. The things I like best about reading books with lots of short stories is that if you don't like one or is getting tired of it, its over withen the chapter. Also it has just great sarcastic/humerous writing throughout it and I feel that keeps it fresh. This book goes through all the stereotypical thoughts about Unicorns and Zombies. Then it steps out into a complete different zone, where you get drunken and or killer unicorns, and zombies that sometimes want mostly brains or is undoubtedly just yearning for true love. Throughout the book before every story there are two people fighting about which is better. There are two teams, team unicorn and team zombie. Each team has about 6 writers a peice that have about 2-3 short stories in the book each. Its becoming and refreshing to have so many writers so I can get a lot of styles in one book. This really is a great read, and somewhat challenging to boot. So the final question is only this, team zombie or team unicorn?</span>
  <a data-text-id="8512002848587783375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6TP/Pva34E6xDqC/7mJHXKgc8HazObWnNTX1NLLmUkFzdWCQwCNmpdqOZ9srNCghEnmoyOLVIatY53FKG+r2tA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VzaNrmAXOy/wHlvzXncB61vrDzKxMb0JBmvCCRCn2YLNcBIAVoO9xJuenJebIW6W4Y5XjODdKQVruUZ3uat9dw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer14991766141161778046">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house </span>
  <span id="freeText14991766141161778046" style="display:none">Holly Black is the #1 New York Times bestselling author of over thirty fantasy novels for kids and teens. She has been a finalist for an Eisner Award and the Lodestar Award, and the recipient of the Mythopoeic Award, a Nebula, and a Newbery Honor. Her books have been translated into 32 languages worldwide and adapted for film. She currently lives in New England with her husband and son in a house with a secret library.</span>

What have zombies ever done to you?<br /><br />Holly: Zombies shamble. I disapprove of shambling. And they have bits that fall off. You never see a unicorn behaving that way.<br /><br />Justine: I shamble. Bits fall off me all the time: hair, skin cells. Are you saying you disapprove of me?&rdquo;</span>
